Quotations from Ma Xiangbo, the Ninety-Three-Year-Old Elder

Changes in World Academic Trends 152

--Fu Ji

The changes in world academic trends over the past sixty years are truly like changes from seas to mulberry fields! Sixty years ago, when studying abroad, from elementary school to middle school, one had to study ancient languages such as Latin and Greek, especially in middle school, where Latin and Greek were required subjects. Similarly, sixty years ago, China was in the era of the Eight-Legged Essay. At that time, scholars had no other knowledge besides literature and art.

In 1880, I went to England. At that time, English academic trends still followed the traditions of the European continent. The English also had to study Latin and Greek. Later, the United States gradually emphasized scientific education. Students intensified the absorption of scientific knowledge, and the study of literature and art gradually declined. Latin and Greek books were no longer read. Until now, elementary and middle schools on the European continent still teach Latin and Greek, but not as much as before. Emphasizing practical learning and downplaying literature and art - this change in academic trends is entirely influenced by modern scientific civilization!

At the same time, our Zeng Wenzhenggong was vigorously promoting his Tongcheng School of Literature, and Wo Ren was vigorously preaching his "ruler, ruler, subject, subject, father, father, son, son..." neo-Confucianism. On the one hand, he advocated policy-oriented literature and art, and on the other hand, he promoted mystical ethics. At that time, the Western powers were gradually spreading eastward. How could the Tongcheng School and neo-Confucianism withstand the tide of scientific civilization? Thus, the Tongcheng School's literature and art and the neo-Confucian School's ethics met the same fate as Greek and Latin.

Western academic trends have reached the era of valuing substance over style, while Chinese academic trends are declining in literature and art, and the substance is even more unimaginable.

Post-War Farmers' Burden 153

--Sun Choucheng

In February of this year, when the 19th Route Army and the 5th Army were working hard to resist the Japanese army in the Shanghai area, the troops near the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou railways were ordered by the government to build defensive works to comply with the slogan of long-term resistance. After the ceasefire agreement was signed in Shanghai, this project was abandoned halfway, leaving only traces. However, the general farmers, limited by government orders, did not dare to demolish them without permission, and suffered endlessly. The situations in Songjiang and Jiaxing are recorded separately as follows.

Outside the South Gate of Songjiang, during the intense fighting in Shanghai, the Ministry of Military Administration sent personnel to survey and designate it as an airfield, specifically enclosing more than 300 mu of farmland. Rivers were filled and fields were leveled. After more than a month of construction, it became a flat land. After the matter ended, the farmers requested its return for cultivation. Then, Li Zuhua, director of the Property Management Office, forwarded it to the Ministry of Military Administration, requesting a swift return to maintain the livelihoods of the farmers. Later, the Ministry replied, saying that it had consulted the Jiangsu Provincial Government to instruct the county to ascertain the number of acres of land, prices, and how to compensate for losses, and to report the details for verification and handling, ordering them to wait quietly. However, on the farmers' side, the farming season has arrived. The return is still awaiting verification, and the fields are not divided. How can they sow? Therefore, they are all worried and hope that officials will not give lip service and resolve it quickly to maintain their livelihoods. Near the towns of Jiaxing, during the Shanghai war, the troops stationed there dug trenches in the fields. Later, after the ceasefire agreement was signed, the troops gradually returned to their original defenses. The Zhejiang Provincial Government feared that farmers would mistakenly believe that these defensive works were no longer needed or would destroy them. Therefore, it specifically ordered the county government to inform the people that if there are defensive works, farmers must cultivate eight feet away from the works before planting rice. Within eight feet, they can only plant cotton and beans to take care of both the defensive works and the livelihoods of the farmers. After receiving the order, the county government immediately forwarded it to the district offices, which forwarded it to the township offices, to notify the farmers to strictly comply. However, according to experienced farmers, the soil quality of paddy fields is suitable for rice but not for cotton. Beans and rice are planted at different times. Although this order seems to take care of the livelihoods of the farmers, in reality, they still suffer endlessly.

History of the Ancient Bell in Zhaofeng Park 154

--Yan Yu

Near the northern part of Zhaofeng Park, in front of a Chinese-style pavilion, there is a large ancient bell, standing steadily on a square stone. Almost all visitors to Zhaofeng Park have seen it.

This large ancient bell is not placed there for the children visiting the park to climb and play on, nor is it used by tourists as photographic material. Of course, if they like to do that, no one will go to stop or interfere, and it is absolutely welcome. However, the only reason why this ancient bell is placed there is because it is worth preserving as a historical monument. This was decided after a heated debate.

This ancient bell was manufactured by an iron factory in New York, USA in 1865 AD. About thirty years ago, the citizens of Shanghai decided to organize a volunteer fire brigade and used the old site of the bell tower on Shandong Road as the central fire brigade station. At that time, this ancient bell, weighing 5,151 pounds, was hung there. A watchman stood on the bell tower every day, looking around for fires. At the same time, there were also sub-stations in the Hongkou and Xinzha areas. At that time, the citizens of Shanghai could know in which area the fire occurred by the number of times the bell rang. As for the ancient bell mentioned in this article, which was hung on the bell tower on Shandong Road, it was stipulated to ring six times whenever a fire occurred in the area.

After twenty years, the bell tower on Shandong Road could not withstand the wind and rain and inevitably showed signs of decay! Later, it even swayed in strong winds. Therefore, it was decided to find a way to remove this ancient bell. This was in 1921. At that time, the question was this: after unloading such a heavy bell, how should it be disposed of? If it were thrown into the Huangpu River, it would be a pity.

At that time, someone suggested placing this ancient bell in the Jing'an Temple International Cemetery. However, the general mourners rose up in opposition, complaining about the annoying sound of the bell. For a while, there was much discussion in society. Many people advocated placing this ancient bell in front of or inside any concession administrative agency. Finally, in October 1922, it was decided to preserve it in Zhaofeng Park, where it is now placed, until today, for visitors to touch and remember!

The diameter of the bottom circumference of this ancient bell is six feet three inches, the height is slightly more than four feet, and the original price was 1,500 US dollars.

Calligraphy, Painting and National Fortune 155

--Han

Calligraphy and painting are minor arts, but the nation's fortune can be glimpsed from them. During the prosperous era of Qianlong and Jiaqing in the Qing Dynasty, calligraphy mostly followed Zhao and Dong, and painting mostly followed the Four Wangs and Wu Yun. The peaceful scene is vividly displayed. By the time of Tongzhi and Guangxu, the nation's fortune had slightly declined. Calligraphers such as Wu Changshuo and Weng Tonghe, and painters such as Zhao Zhiqian and Ren Bonian, all valued style and strength, and the meaning of elegance and nobility was lost. Descending to the present day, it is getting worse and worse. In calligraphy, only Northern Wei is revered. In painting, only Bada Shanren and Shi Tao are valued. The disjointed and strange talk cannot be investigated. This is indeed a hidden worry for those who care about the world's affairs. Yesterday, following the invitation of a friend, I drove to the Yihai Huilan Society in Ci'an Lane, Ningbo Road, to visit the fan painting exhibition. After looking at it, I felt gratified. The atmosphere of the art world has recovered from decline to prosperity. The habit of wild scribbling with a rough brush has become almost non-existent. Unexpectedly, at the end of Yongjia, I heard the sound of Zhengshi again. The ancients' words are suitable to be given to this occasion. Since calligraphy and painting are related to national fortune, at this time of national turmoil, the calligraphy and painting circles can have such a good image. When decline reaches its extreme, prosperity will return. When the negative is exhausted, the positive begins. I will see it at the Yihai Huilan Society.

Short News: Cheng Yanqiu toured Berlin on May 10th. The League of Nations Education Delegation, Pei, opened a banquet for him and introduced the managers of the major drama and music academies in Berlin. He visited them on different days. Students studying in Germany also held a welcome on the 16th. The Far East Association held a grand tea party on the 21st. Guests requested Mr. Cheng to sing Chinese opera. He declined because he did not bring a pianist. They all said that no accompaniment was necessary, but only a solo performance. Then he sang a section of "Tears of Desolation". Before singing, Linde explained that it was a non-war and peace drama. The audience clapped and welcomed him, requesting another song. Then he sang a few lines from "Scolding the Temple". The whole audience praised it. Cheng decided to stay for two months and visit other countries because he was busy with social engagements and the survey was not completed.

World News in Brief 156

--Haike

Greta Garbo, who has caused a sensation in the world as a movie star in the United States, Crelagarb was originally from Sweden. When she first arrived in the United States, no one paid attention to her. The first time she signed a contract with a film company, her weekly salary was only 15 British pounds.

Milliners in Europe and America have come up with a novel idea and are competing to use horse mane to make fashionable women's hats. They are chosen for their lightness and loveliness, but are more expensive than all straw hats. It is now fashionable in Western social circles.

A British naturalist said that there are several kinds of animals that never show signs of aging, so their age cannot be estimated from their appearance, such as fish and snakes. There are many such examples.

Going to bed too late at night can cause rheumatism. Thirty thousand children in London suffer from this disease because their parents do not pay attention to their sleeping time and let them go to bed late.

Recently, the capital of Hungary, Budapest, has been plagued by sparrows, which fly around everywhere. Therefore, after nightfall, men hold long poles, walk back and forth on tree-lined roads, and release explosives into the thickets to scare them away.

Impressions of Qingdao (Part 2) 157

--He Gongchao

Between men and women, there is only a plank wall separating them. It is not high. If someone who is eager to appreciate the beauty of the opposite sex's body stands on tiptoe while leaning against the top of the wall, he can definitely see his fill. However, there are probably no such brave people now.

Although the facilities in such a bathroom are simple, they are cleaned very thoroughly. In addition, there are also bathhouses with more complete and exquisite arrangements, but Chinese people are not allowed to enter. In Qingdao, there are many things that "Chinese are not allowed to enter..." Japanese sell heroin, open opium dens, and smuggle military supplies. Chinese police are not allowed to arrest them. No Chinese soldiers are allowed to be stationed in the city. This year, during the cherry blossom season at the Japanese shrine, Chinese people are not allowed to visit (probably to vent their debts for the Shanghai War):... It is more than just this small bathhouse. I heard that in Tokyo, where the cost of living is so high, bathhouses charge only a few cents.

The Destroyer of Parks: When the seaside park was first completed, many well-lit and expensive light bulbs were installed in the park. However, they were often smashed by stones thrown by unknown people. You install them once, and they break them once. This brutal destroyer probably uses these public properties as targets to practice his own eyesight.

The authorities once offered a reward for this matter, offering 50 yuan to anyone who catches this destroyer, but no one was caught. Why does this brutal destroyer want to destroy these public properties that belong to the public? What kind of perverted psychology does he have? Alas! From this point, I see a despicable nature in the Chinese national character that is shameful to speak of, that is, the nature of taking pleasure in cruelty and entertaining oneself with destruction. Seeing a person (especially a woman) slip and fall in the middle of the street, the shopkeepers on both sides laugh out loud, even clapping and laughing, and no one wants to go over and help him up. Similarly, when the swaggering generals defeat the enemy's army, causing blood to flow like rivers, and return in triumph to receive the compliments of their colleagues, a smile appears on the corners of their mouths based on this cruel psychology.

If this kind of cruel psychology is not removed from the hearts of every individual in the entire nation, will China one day become a peaceful and humane country? I am very doubtful.

Record of Dual Military and Literary Life (94) 158

— Master of the Studio Seeking Happiness

Chapter Eleven: A Modest Town Awaits the Commander's Banner, Humble Crowds Humble Attend the Retinue

These people, upon hearing that Commander An's background was so significant, and that Fourth Master Wu had been honored as Commander An's only trusted chief of staff, were naturally both astonished and admiring. They flocked to flatter and congratulate Fourth Master Wu, saying, "With Fourth Master's talents, you are unmatched in our county. Everyone believed that you would rise to prominence sooner or later. Who would have thought that you would ascend so quickly, and now you have been promoted to chief of staff in one fell swoop? Our entire county will surely benefit from your light, Fourth Master. Although we lack great abilities and are not worthy of holding your horse or assisting you, if there is anything we can do to help you in this area, Fourth Master, please just give us your orders. Surely, we should be wholeheartedly loyal and serve you, even if it means running errands and doing small tasks?" Fourth Master Wu, being vigorously flattered by them, immediately became elated and lost his sense of proportion. He invited them all to help, promising them various commissions, and raised a jumble of suggestions for pacification matters. Among them were civil servants from the county government, so it was easy to talk about the county government. They suggested that everything could be handled by informing the county magistrate to deal with official business, which would be very convenient. But as soon as Fourth Master Wu heard the words "county magistrate," his eyebrows suddenly shot up, and flames of anger erupted from his forehead. He slammed the table furiously and cursed, "Are you talking about that old dog, County Magistrate Li Pinzhai? Hmph. Hmph. Now I don't need him. He's not fit to be an official anymore. It's my turn to deal with him and eliminate the hatred in my heart, and let him know who I, Wu Siye, am!" As soon as these words came out, the others were taken aback and looked at each other. Although they were eager to know the root cause of this inside story, they were intimidated by Fourth Master Wu's power and dared not ask rashly. Who knew that Fourth Master Wu, in his expansive mood, couldn't keep his mouth shut and lightly told them everything. "I, surnamed Wu, am a straightforward person and don't do things in secret. To be honest, the reason I went to the provincial capital this time was because that old dog Li Pinzhai looked down on people too much. He only knew how to be lawless and arbitrarily set up rules to demand money, but he didn't care about the local gentry at all. Others can tolerate it, but I, Fourth Master Wu, who has always mediated lawsuits for people and made a golden reputation, cannot tolerate him casually ruining my good meal ticket. Going to the provincial capital, I was prepared to fight him to the death, to go to both the military and civilian yamen to sue him."

Local News

Yesterday's Memorial Service for Martyrs from Both Railways 159

Minister of Railways Gu Mengyu Presided over the Ceremony

Groundbreaking Ceremony for the Monument Held in the Afternoon

On the evening of January 28th, the Japanese army suddenly launched an invasion of Zhabei. Our defending troops fought bravely and resisted for more than a month, withdrawing completely. The soldiers' loyalty and bravery for the country are admirable. The Japanese plan was to seize the railway station in one battle, driving straight in to force our surrender. The importance of Shanghai North Station in this battle was not limited to the transportation of supplies to the rear and the deployment of soldiers to the front lines. The Japanese plan failed, so they dispatched planes to bomb North Station to block our transportation and cut off our communication. However, all the railway employees, amidst the smoke and fire, still had a patriotic heart to defend the country. Some even served day and night, without rest for five days and nights. Many also sacrificed their lives under the enemy's atrocities. Therefore, the two railway administrations held a memorial service yesterday morning at 10:00 AM to comfort the loyal souls of the martyrs. The monument will be built next to the Paotaiwan Station and the groundbreaking ceremony was held there yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM. The railway administration provided a special train for representatives from all walks of life to attend. The construction of the monument will begin within days. The details are recorded below:

Memorial Archway at the Memorial Service (Photo by Li Zunyong) 160

Details of the Memorial Service 161

Arrangement of the Venue: The venue was in the open space east of North Station. A temporary bamboo shed was erected, with a plain white archway in front. There were horizontal plaques with inscriptions by Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, "Sacrifice for the Country," and Chen Xinghan, "Public Loyalty and Service to the Country." Below was a banner that read, "Memorial Service for Railway Employees Sacrificed in the National Crisis." Mourning couplets were hung on both sides of the gate, all the way to Baoshan Road. The venue was also filled with mourning couplets. The altar was in the center of the north end, with the Party and National emblem and the portrait of Sun Yat-sen, as well as the portraits of the martyred employees. The altar table was set with flowers and spirit tablets, inscribed with "The Spirit Tablets of Railway Employees Sacrificed in the National Crisis." In front of the tablets were offerings. The flower wreaths presented by Chiang Guangnai, Cai Tingkai, and others were placed in front of the altar. To the right of the altar was the seating area for the families of the martyred employees, and in front of it was the military band. To the left of the altar was the seating area for the representatives attending the ceremony, and in front of it was the seating area for the guests.

Attendees: Including Minister of Railways Gu Mengyu, Counselor of the Ministry of Railways Gu Zhengding, Mayor Wu's representative Chen Kecheng, Shanghai Chamber of Commerce representative Wang Xiaolai, High Court representative Shen Jiayi, Local Court representative Wang Xun, International Trade Bureau representative Cao Sen, Social Affairs Bureau representative Hou Dachun, as well as the directors of the two railway administrations, Chen Xinghan, Chief of the Transportation Department Zheng Baozhao, and over a thousand representatives from all walks of life.

Memorial Ceremony: As the clock struck ten, the whistle sounded mournfully. The master of ceremonies announced the start of the ceremony. The presiding officer, assistant officers, representatives from various organizations, and guests entered the hall one after another. Everyone stood in solemn silence. First, the music band of the Municipal Public Security Bureau played funeral music, sang the Party song, and performed the rituals. Then, they bowed three times to the portraits of the martyred heroes, and observed three minutes of silence. At this time, the alarm bell rang loudly, shaking people's hearts, and the cries of the martyrs' families could also be faintly heard. Then, the presiding officer Gu Mengyu delivered a eulogy (recorded below) and presented flower wreaths. Representatives from various organizations offered sacrifices and read eulogies. Then, Min Luoheng, the representative of the two railway administrations' Party headquarters, reported on the circumstances of the martyrs' deaths. Wang Xiaolai and others gave heartfelt speeches. Finally, they shouted slogans, took photos, and the ceremony ended.

Presiding Officer's Eulogy: Presiding officer Gu Mengyu delivered a eulogy, saying, "Today, colleagues from the two railway administrations are mourning the employees who sacrificed themselves in the national crisis. We are deeply saddened. Recalling the suffering of the martyrs when they sacrificed themselves, we are even more mournful. The martyrs' death in the national crisis is very great and cannot be compared with death in disasters or robberies. It is said that death can be lighter than a feather or heavier than Mount Tai. The martyrs' death in protecting the railway can be said to be heavier than Mount Tai. As we mourn here, we should always remember the martyrs' great sacrifice and strive to recover the lost territory and coexist with the country. Therefore, in today's memorial service, in addition to mourning the dead, the living should work harder."

Assistant Officer's Report: Min Luoheng, the representative of the two railway administrations' Party headquarters, on behalf of the directors of the two railway administrations, Chen Xinghan, reported on the details of the martyrs' deaths, saying, "Since the January 28th Incident, colleagues from the two railway administrations have felt that serving the railway this time is completely different from serving during previous civil wars. Therefore, everyone was determined and, with a spirit of fearlessness, tried their best to protect the railway. The railway administration had made considerable preparations before the outbreak of the war, so they did not feel very difficult after the incident. During the fierce fighting between the two sides, our colleagues from the two railway administrations bravely entered the hail of bullets and artillery fire. The Japanese army's weapons were sharp and their artillery fire was fierce. Therefore, twelve employees of our two railway administrations died under Japanese guns, artillery, and bombs, sixteen were injured, and twelve were missing (list of deaths, injuries, and missing persons below). There are still some who have not been identified due to time constraints. In short, the service spirit and great sacrifice of our colleagues from the two railway administrations this time are truly worthy of mourning."

Guest Speeches: Shanghai Chamber of Commerce representative Wang Xiaolai said in his speech, "In this sad memorial service, the cries of grief and suffering from the families of the martyrs are truly heartbreaking and make it impossible to speak. The martyrs of the two railway administrations sacrificed their lives for the country, dying for the sake of the living. Their death is glorious and great, and will be remembered forever. The martyrs are dead, but how will the living work hard to comfort the dead in the afterlife?" After Mr. Wang finished his speech, representatives from the Zhabei Chamber of Commerce Federation also gave heartfelt speeches.

Families of the Victims (Photo by Xu Tianzhang) 162

Cries in the Venue: Most of the families of the martyred employees also participated in the memorial service. After arriving at the venue, they were located on the right side of the stage. There were elderly people with white hair, young women with red faces, and young children. When they entered the venue, their eyes were already swollen and red from crying. When the eulogy was read, the tone was gentle and mournful, like weeping, which aroused the sorrow of the families of the victims. Sobbing uncontrollably, they burst into loud wails. The guests who heard them also felt sympathy and wiped away tears of compassion.

Groundbreaking Ceremony for the Monument 163

Special Train to Wusong: Over 300 assistant officers, representatives from various organizations, guests, and families of the martyrs went to Wusong Station after the ceremony. They boarded several special trains prepared by the railway administration in advance. They were warmly received by the reception staff and provided with tea and refreshments. At 1:15 PM, the special train headed straight to Wusong. At 1:45 PM, it arrived at Paotaiwan Station. They got off the train one after another and walked to the site a few steps in front of the station.

Order of the Groundbreaking Ceremony: (1) Gathering, (2) Officials for the groundbreaking ceremony take their seats, (3) Representatives from various organizations take their seats, (4) Guests take their seats, (5) Standing in solemn silence, (6) Bowing three times to the Party and National flag and the portrait of Sun Yat-sen, (7) Three minutes of silence, (8) Groundbreaking ceremony performed by the officials, (9) Ceremony concluded, (10) Photographing.

Performing the Groundbreaking Ceremony: After the guests arrived at the site, they encircled the base in a circle. At exactly 2:00 PM, Chen Xinghan, the official for the groundbreaking ceremony, walked to the center of the base, took a hoe, loosened the soil, and the ceremony was completed. While Mr. Chen was performing the ceremony, the families of the martyrs cried loudly again, even prostrating on the ground and unable to get up. They were later comforted by the railway administration staff before they stopped. At 3:00 PM, they returned to Shanghai by the original train.

Groundbreaking Ceremony for the Monument (Photo by Xu Tianzhang) 164

Building the Monument: The design of the monument has not yet been finalized. It will generally be a white stone base, with a square stone pillar on top. Bronze plates will be inlaid on the front and back. The front will have the four characters "Sacrifice for the Country" personally inscribed by Commander Cai Tingkai, three feet high and about two feet wide. The back will have the names of the martyred employees and their families. The two sides may be inscribed with prefaces personally written by the directors of the two railway administrations to commemorate them. The location has been designated in front of the Paotaiwan Road Police Training Institute, with ten acres of land set aside as a garden to be planted with flowers and trees for decoration. The monument will be in the center of the garden. The buildings of the training institute have been destroyed in the war and may be rebuilt as a memorial hall to display portraits and relics for future generations to pay their respects, and for tourists to rest. The cost of building the monument has been decided to be allocated 10,000 yuan from the public welfare fund of the employees of the two railway administrations. If the cost of building the memorial hall is insufficient, more funds can be allocated. In the future, the new Shanghai-Nanjing Station will also have a special room to display commemorative items.

Comforting the Survivors: After the groundbreaking ceremony, the directors of the two railway administrations, Chen Xinghan, expressed his condolences to the families of all the martyred employees and reported on the measures for comforting the survivors, saying, "After the September 18th Incident, some employees of the Beining Railway were injured or killed in the line of duty. The railway administration then submitted a request to the Ministry of Railways for preferential compensation. The Ministry then issued the Beining Railway Compensation Measures for Railway Employees Martyred in the Line of Duty, which were quite generous. When the January 28th Incident occurred, the two railway administrations were in the line of fire. The service of the employees of the two railway administrations was very dangerous. Therefore, the Ministry of Railways issued the same measures to the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administrations for reference. The regulations stipulate that in addition to providing clothing, coffins, and compensation, the original salary of the martyred employees will be increased by one grade and given to the direct relatives of the deceased. Their children can also attend schools run by the railway administration for free. If they want to pursue further studies after graduating from the primary school there, the railway administration can also sponsor their studies. If their wives and daughters want to find a job to support their lives, the railway administration can also help them find a job. Those who are injured and disabled and want to do light work will still be employed by the railway administration and paid their original salary. Those who are unable to work will be given preferential treatment in accordance with the compensation measures."

Statistics of Deaths and Injuries: The statistics of the martyred employees of the two railway administrations are listed below: Twelve dead, including Ji Youqing, Ye Keqing, Zhang Jinbin, Xu Bin, Wang Jingxian, Gao Shaoquan, Zhang Shengrong, Xue Sanlang, Zhu Yonglin, Xuan Quanduo, Luo Yi, and Hu Dejuan. Sixteen injured, including Dong Yifeng, Tang Xudong, Wang Pin, Chen Decheng, Wu Xiangshan, Wang Qichang, Wu Zhonglun, Qiu Zhiyuan, Yang Gumin, Li Jingsheng, Jiang Guochen, Zheng Daqi, Zhu Yaoqing, Pan Bingquan, Chen Pingzhang, and Tang Asan. Twenty-two missing, including Gao Weixiong, Yang Yuyu, Fan Hongsheng, Li Jintang, Chen Ergou, Li Shoushen, Qiu Jinzhang, Zhang Haiquan, Xiao Asan, Shen Huochun, Yang Baoquan, Zhang Dashuang, Yan Xiaomao, Yao Zanxing, Shen Yanglang, Liang Bingfa, Fan Yibao, Zhang Wenkui, Tian Rongfu, Song Changfa, and Fan Wenhan.

No Reply Yet from Japan Regarding Troop Withdrawal from District D Yesterday 165

Our side reported to the chairman of the joint committee and notified Okazaki of the withdrawal of Japanese troops from District D and the three cotton mills of Huafeng, Toyota, and Gongda. At 9:00 AM the day before yesterday, Yu Hongjun, a member of the joint committee, urged Okazaki. Okazaki also replied to our side at 11:00 AM, saying that a formal reply could be given yesterday afternoon. However, no reply was received from Okazaki all day yesterday. Mr. Yu believed that the Japanese side was showing too little sincerity and reported the situation to the chairman of the joint committee, Sterling, in a letter at 3:00 PM, asking him to pay attention to the inquiry. At the same time, he also invited Okazaki to meet at the joint committee and notified the Japanese side in writing of the report to the chairman. Therefore, this issue will depend on whether Sterling can urge the Japanese side to show sincerity in a short period of time. Otherwise, the joint committee will hold a major meeting to resolve this outstanding issue. The details are recorded below:

Report to the Chairman: Yesterday, joint committee member Yu Hongjun, in accordance with Okazaki's previous appointment, waited quietly until 12:00 PM. Seeing that the Japanese side had not replied, he decided to report the Japanese side's repeated procrastination and breach of contract to the chairman of the joint committee, Sterling, asking him to inquire and urge the Japanese side. The original letter was personally delivered by Mr. Yu's secretary, Langge, at 3:00 PM yesterday. The content of the letter was roughly as follows: "Regarding the Japanese troops in the three cotton mills of Huafeng, Toyota, and Gongda, and District D, although the Japanese side has repeatedly stated that they will withdraw, as of June 28, there has been no sincere indication of a definite date for withdrawal. The situation in this city has long returned to its state before the January 28th Incident. There is no possibility for the Japanese troops to linger any longer. According to the ceasefire agreement, all Japanese troops in Shanghai should have been withdrawn within four weeks. At that time, the Chinese government authorities, considering the large number of Japanese troops in Shanghai, were afraid that they would not be able to withdraw completely in a short time, so they agreed to have four temporary garrison areas as a temporary arrangement for the Japanese troops. This move was for the sake of the Japanese troops. Today, the Japanese troops are lingering and procrastinating repeatedly, which has violated the spirit of the agreement. Please, Mr. Chairman, investigate the situation and pay attention to it, and urge the Japanese side to fulfill the agreement as soon as possible and withdraw the Japanese troops from the above-mentioned locations as soon as possible."

Notify Okazaki: At the same time, Mr. Yu invited the Japanese representative Okazaki to meet and notified Okazaki of the report to the chairman of the joint committee. In addition to the verbal statement, he also handed over to Okazaki a letter prepared in advance to notify the Japanese side. The content of the notice stated that the reason why our side reported to the chairman of the joint committee was due to your side's lack of sincerity and violation of the agreement. However, on the one hand, we still hope that your representative can continue to urge the naval marine corps authorities to withdraw as soon as possible within days. At that time, Okazaki, after receiving this written and verbal notice, expressed that the Japanese naval marine corps was preparing and would urge again, and promised to reply to our side immediately. The talks ended at 5:00 PM.

Final Resolution: The future progress of this issue will depend on the Japanese side's reaction after Sterling urges the Japanese side, and on whether Okazaki will give our side a satisfactory reply within days. Therefore, it is expected that if the Japanese side shows no sincerity again, Sterling will convene a meeting of the joint committee in his capacity as chairman to discuss the matter. At the same time, according to Mr. Yu Hongjun's words to the New Sound News Agency, if the Japanese side disregards the treaty and still gives no definite reply, I will also request the joint committee to hold a meeting to discuss and resolve the matter.

Great Flood in the Yangtze River, Wuhan Will Not Suffer Disaster 167

Hunan is Also Building Dykes

A Glimpse of Flood Control Work

Xi Dejiong's Statement

In the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, the plum rains have not stopped for days, and the river water has surged. Many places in Hunan and Jiangxi have been flooded and breached. This matter has been repeatedly recorded in this newspaper. The water level in Hankou has exceeded 38 feet, and people are increasingly afraid, deeply worried that they will see the disaster of the land sinking again this year. Reporters went to the Flood Relief Committee yesterday to meet with Mr. Xi Dejiong, chief engineer of the Engineering and Relief Office, and Mr. Zhou Houkun, and others, to inquire about the flood situation in the Yangtze River. According to Mr. Xi, the recent flooding in Hunan and Hubei is due to the continuous heavy rains, which have caused the river water to rise. However, a water level of 38 feet is common. The reason why people are afraid this year is because of the disaster last year. The long dykes along the Yangtze River have been completed, starting from Jingjiang and ending at Cihu River in Zhenjiang. The dykes along the river will be completed, and their height will be three feet higher than the highest water level last year. Compared with the current water level, the difference is still large. The dykes in Hankou are three feet higher than the 52 feet when the land was flooded last year, which is 55 feet. Now it is only 38 and a half feet, which is 16 and a half feet away. We can be sure that there will not be a repeat of the tragedy of last year. If there were no newly built dykes, some places along the river might have been flooded already. As for the Zhanggong Dyke project in Hankou, it was transferred from the Engineering and Relief Office to the Wuhan Water Conservancy Engineering Bureau for construction. The Engineering and Relief Office is only subsidizing relief wheat. Regarding Hunan, such as Changsha, Yiyang, and Changde, there are reports that they have already been flooded. The terrain of the above places is very low-lying, and it is easy to be flooded when the river water rises slightly. The Flood Relief Committee and the Engineering and Relief Office have also allocated a large amount of relief wheat, more than 17,000 tons, to the Xiangjiang and Yuanjiang Rivers to carry out engineering relief and build dykes. The Tenth District Engineering Bureau was established in Changsha, entrusted to Mr. Tan Changkai to manage the engineering relief and dyke construction in Hunan. From Lulin Dyke to Xiangyin, Changde, and Yiyang, which surrounds the lake, to Wanzi Lake, a total of 376 kilometers of dykes have been built. After the completion of this project, the Xiangjiang and Yuanjiang Rivers will be able to avoid the flood of water forever. As for the river dykes built in Hankou, from Ertaokou in the north to Dajun Mountain, and from the opposite bank of Wuxue in the south to Jinkou, connecting Jiangxi and linking Chenglingji in the upper reaches, a total of 421 kilometers, which were managed by engineer He Baochu, have now been completely completed. Therefore, Wuhan can be guaranteed not to have another major flood this year.

Zhu Qinglan's Report on Flood Relief 168

Zhu Qinglan, permanent member of the National Government's Flood Relief Committee and director of the disaster area working group, reported that in the summer of the 20th year, the heavens sent floods and people lost their defenses, resulting in the devastation of eighteen provinces. Qinglan was appointed to work in the disaster area and will end his term in ten months. I dare to extract the essentials to report to you all. Qinglan has been handling drought relief in the provinces of North China, Lu, Ji, Yu, and Shan for seven years, although the area is smaller, the collection of comrades and their own energy, still can barely gather, as for the size of this disaster area, the severity of the disaster, it has not been seen in hundreds of years, so its relief is not easy, it must be known to the world, relief funds, talents, time, are all related and essential. Therefore, according to its situation, the work is divided into three parts, namely emergency relief, engineering relief, and agricultural relief, emergency relief offices, engineering relief offices, and agricultural relief offices are set up, and then the transportation of relief wheat is regarded as the element of three relief, and the transportation and storage offices are added, and in order to prevent the occurrence of corruption in all parts, an inspection office is added. (To be continued)

The Bureau of Public Works Submits a Petition to the Municipal Government to Continue the Downtown Project 172

Establishment of a Committee to Manage Funds for the Construction of the Downtown Area

The Municipal Government’s New Building and Roads Within the Concession Will Resume Work

Recently, as the order of the city gradually returns to normal, the Municipal Government has decided to continue the construction of the downtown area according to the original plan and steps. The matter has been discussed and resolved in the Municipal Council. It is now known that the Bureau of Public Works has notified the contractors to prepare for the resumption of work on the Municipal Government’s new building and road projects within the first phase of the concession. It is expected that the original state will be restored within the next month. In addition, the Municipal Government has notified the concessionaires to elect representatives so that the committee for the management of construction funds for the downtown area can be established as soon as possible. According to the original plan, the outstanding quarter of the land price was to be paid in full within four months of receiving the land. This deadline has long passed. However, out of consideration, the Municipal Government has revised the plan. Starting from July 1st, the payment will be made in three installments, with two months for each installment, and each installment will be a quarter of the land price. The original document submitted by the Bureau of Public Works to the Municipal Government is recorded below. It is submitted for the continued development of the downtown area construction project. Respectfully presenting our humble opinions, we request your review and deliberation. We believe that the downtown construction plan has long attracted the attention of both Chinese and foreigners. For the past three years, we have worked diligently, sparing no effort. Although it is not yet fully complete, it has already taken shape. To name a few major projects, such as the construction of the Municipal Government’s new building and the paving of important trunk roads, some are halfway completed, and others are nearing completion. This year, the sudden outbreak of the incident caused the area to become a war zone, and all projects were suspended. Recently, various parties have been discussing the reconstruction of the war zone, and the relocation of the North Railway Station may gradually become a reality. Compared to the so-called reconstruction of the war zone, rather than focusing on partial reorganization, it would be better to take a holistic approach and make fundamental improvements. Otherwise, the Zhabei and Jiangwan areas before the war were extremely narrow and crude. Even if they were restored to their former state, what would be worth praising? Therefore, to seek prosperity in Zhabei, the North Railway Station must first be moved to a suitable location. To see a rapid revitalization of Jiangwan and Wusong, the downtown plan must be continued. This is the only way to rebuild the war zone, and this can be asserted. Now, regarding the various points that should be addressed in the downtown area, they are listed as follows: (1) Continue the construction of the Municipal Government’s new building (this point has been submitted separately for instructions). (2) Continue the excavation and earthwork for roads within the first phase of the downtown concession. (3) Establish a committee for the management of construction funds for the downtown area and urge the payment of land prices. It is found that three-quarters of the land price remains unpaid. Given the current situation, it may be advisable to change the original plan and re-establish a method for phased payments. As for the concessionaires, the regulation requiring construction to begin within one year of receiving the land should also be extended as appropriate to show flexibility. The above three matters are all urgent tasks. If we do not catch up quickly and devote all our efforts, the grand Shanghai construction plan will have no hope of realization. The Municipal Government’s efforts in the area over the years will be in vain, and the achievements will be lost. It would be a pity. Therefore, we present our humble opinions and respectfully request your review and deliberation. This would be in the public interest. Respectfully submitted to the Mayor.

New Uniforms Issued to the City Security Force 173

On July 1st, the Municipal Government, considering the special circumstances of the city, believed that the local defense could not be handled solely by the police force. Therefore, the proposal to organize a city security force was made. Preparations have been underway for over a month, and now it is largely in order. Regarding the uniforms, submissions have been made to the central government ministries. Recently, a reply was received from the Ministry of Interior, temporarily approving the record. It is now learned that the Municipal Government has completed the tailoring of the aforementioned uniforms and will distribute them to the officers and soldiers of the various units for use on July 1st. The illustrations of the uniforms are attached below.

Illustrations of the Shanghai City Security Force Uniforms (A) 174

Officer Uniforms: The summer hat is made of khaki twill fabric (Western name: khaki drill), and the winter hat can be made of khaki wool. The hat wall is surrounded by a black band with a woven pattern. The strap in front of the brim is made of black lacquered leather for lieutenants, silver woven tape for field officers, and the same for generals. The brim of the hat is made of black lacquered leather for lieutenants, and field officers and above have a silver edge two fen wide along the edge of the brim. The hat badge is located in the center of the black band on the hat wall, made of copper and plated with a magnetic enamel blue sky and white sun national emblem. The summer coat is made of khaki twill fabric, and the winter coat is made of khaki wool. It is a Zhongshan suit with a notched lapel and collar badges to indicate rank. There are shoulder straps to indicate the unit name. The sleeves have cuffs, but no insignia. There are four pockets on the front of the chest, each closed with a button. The coat has a straight front with five copper buttons. The outer trousers are made of the same material as the outer coat, in the style of riding breeches to facilitate riding. The left shoulder strap is decorated with the copper characters "Shanghai City," and the right shoulder strap is decorated with the copper characters "Security Force." The collar badges for third-class lieutenants have a black velvet base with silver or white borders, a horizontal line four fen wide, and one silver border, with one to three gilt copper stars depending on the rank. The collar badges for third-class field officers are the same as those for field officers, but with one silver border in the middle to distinguish them. The collar badges for generals are all silver with silver borders and gold stars, the number of stars depending on the rank. Generals and field officers wear long black leather boots, and lieutenants wear short black leather boots. Officers use pistols, and the ammunition pouches are made of yellow hard leather and are not used during ceremonies. Officers use pistol belts, and the pouches are made of yellow hard leather and are not used during ceremonies. Officers use sword belts, made of yellow thick leather, used for wearing pistols during training and swords during ceremonies. Lieutenants use white canvas leggings over the leather boots, covering the top of the boots. (B) Enlisted Men's Uniforms: The summer hat is made of khaki twill fabric, and the hat wall is surrounded by a black cloth band. The hat strap and brim are made of black lacquered leather. The hat badge is made of copper and plated with a magnetic enamel blue sky and white sun national emblem. The summer coat is made of khaki twill fabric, and the winter coat is made of the same color wool. It has collar badges to indicate the regiment number, unit number, and serial number. There are shoulder straps to indicate the unit name. Soldiers have sleeve insignia to indicate rank. The outer trousers are made of the same material as the outer coat, in the style of simple riding breeches to facilitate kneeling and lying during shooting. The left collar badge shows the regiment number in Arabic numerals and the battalion number in English letters, both made of copper. The right collar badge marks the personal serial number in Arabic numerals. The left shoulder strap is decorated with the copper characters "Shanghai City," and the right shoulder strap is decorated with the copper characters "Security Force." The sleeve insignia is made of khaki twill fabric with a half-inch wide right-angled silver braid. Sergeants first class have three stripes, sergeants have two stripes, and corporals have one stripe. The belt is made of yellow thick leather, adjustable in length, with a copper buckle engraved with the characters "Security Force." The short leather boots are made of black leather. The leggings are made of white canvas, covering the top of the leather boots.

Mortar Test Fired in Longhua 175

Song Ziwen Personally Attends the Observation. The Longhua Garrison Headquarters announced that mortar tests were conducted at the airfield yesterday afternoon. The mortars were German-made and managed by Kong Shiyang Trading Company on Jiangxi Road in the city. Therefore, yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM, the trading company used the French Concession Public Works Bureau's vehicles to transport two mortars (one for reserve). The accompanying French personnel arranged and placed them properly at the airfield. The targets were placed in Shandong Province, along the nearby Pujiang Airfield. The Garrison Headquarters first sent personnel to liaise with Sun Liren, the head of the Tax Police Regiment. By 2:30 PM, those who came to observe the test firing included Minister of Finance Song Ziwen, Song Ziliang, Song Zian, former Hangzhou Mayor Zhou Xiangxian, Garrison Headquarters staff officers Zheng Youshang and Gu Gaodi, and the Tax Police Regiment commander's staff, including foreigners, totaling fifty or sixty people. A total of twenty rounds were fired, each round hitting the target. The results were excellent. Moreover, the mortars were equipped with movable supports and rangefinders, which were more responsive and complete than previous models. The test ended at 3:30 PM, and everyone dispersed.

Record of the Establishment of the China Aviation Construction Association 176

The China Aviation Construction Association was organized and prepared by leaders from all sectors of the city. Its purpose is to promote aviation construction and cultivate aviation talents. The preparations for the association have been completed, and the inaugural meeting was held yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM.

Representatives Attending: Xu Shiying, Li Gang, Xiong Xiling, Zhu Ziqiao, Zha Liangzhao, Weng Zhaojing, Qiu Guozhen, Shen Dexie, Yin Zhiling, Li Cishan, Chen Liting, Wang Chengzhi, Liu Shixiong, Tan Bozhi, Jiang Jiemin, Chu Huiseng, Wu Shan, Lin Yunshan, Huang Menggui, and more than seventy others were publicly elected Yin Zhiling as chairman and Tao Shuyuan as recorder.

Meeting Details: The meeting was called to order at 4:30 PM. (1) Chairman Yin Zhiling delivered the opening speech. (2) Initiator Li Cishan reported on the progress of the preparations. (3) Speeches were given by Qiu Guozhen, Chief of Staff of the 156th Brigade of the 19th Route Army, Shen Dexie, Director of the Shanghai Aircraft Factory, Huang Menggui, Lin Yunfan, and others. (4) Discussion of the articles of association. (5) Election of directors. (6) Refreshments. (7) Adjournment.

Excerpts from Speeches: Qiu Guozhen briefly stated that the Japanese once boasted that they had one thousand aircraft, enough to destroy China. In light of the facts, China certainly does not have aircraft capable of defending the airspace. The existing aircraft are not only structurally unsound and difficult to transport, but also have limited flight time. If the aircraft is flown for too long, the parts may be damaged, making it impossible to fly, let alone fight. Therefore, the business of manufacturing aircraft must be vigorously promoted. He also cited the various constraints faced during the anti-Japanese war. (2) Shen Dexie said that it is easy for Europe and the United States to manufacture aircraft, but difficult for China to manufacture its own aircraft because of the lack of materials and talent. Therefore, it is appropriate to establish factories with Chinese and foreign joint ventures to manufacture aircraft. Air defense requires various types of aircraft, such as fighter planes, bombers, attack aircraft, and reconnaissance aircraft. China has no more than five aircraft that can be used for air defense. Furthermore, they are all concentrated in Nanjing. During the anti-Japanese war, some people questioned why naval aircraft could not be used in combat. However, they did not know that the naval aircraft were only training aircraft. They had no machine guns or bomb racks. Therefore, the only way to avoid unnecessary sacrifices was to move these aircraft elsewhere. Regarding the promotion of the aviation industry, the government may not have the resources or the desire to be comprehensive. If the public can invest in setting up factories, there is a precedent in foreign countries for governments to purchase aircraft from private aircraft factories. Although this is a new undertaking in China, it may be a way to promote production and defend the country. (3) Huang Mengshu reported on the efforts of overseas Chinese to promote aviation construction in their homeland.

Discussion of the Articles of Association: The association's articles of association consist of twelve articles. Five articles were passed yesterday, but due to the lateness of the hour, Tan Bozhi, Yin Zhiling, and Zheng Xitao were appointed to review the entire text and submit it to the first plenary meeting of the board of directors for approval.

Election of Directors: Next, according to the articles of association, thirty-one directors of the first session were elected. The list of elected directors is as follows: Zhu Qinglan, Shi Liangcai, Wang Xiaoyao, Xu Jingren, Xiong Bingren, Chen Lianbo, Wen Zongyao, Chu Huiseng, Yan Zhifang, Yin Zhiling, He Dong, Feng Shaoshan, Wu Shan, Tan Bozhi, Huang Mengshu, Qian Xinzhi, Zhang Gongquan, Hu Yunqiu, Li Cishan, Zheng Xitao, Zhang Zhuping, Shen Dexie, He Jiacheng, Lin Kanghou, Lin Yunfan, Luo Yinqian, Wang Chengzhi, Zhu Lin, Zheng Zhengqiu. (Note: The names of two directors are temporarily not announced.)

The Silk Factory Strike in Hongkou Was Heard Yesterday 177

Labor and Management Held Separate Meetings

Central Government Dispatched Special Personnel to Investigate

Since the silk factories in the Hongkou district successively declared strikes, representatives sent by the labor unions negotiated with the factory owners, but no solution has been reached. Yesterday, both the labor unions and the factory owners convened meetings to discuss the matter. The details are recorded separately below.

Report to the Party Headquarters: The Fourth District Silk Industry Workers' Union yesterday reported to the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Bureau of Social Affairs, reporting the truth about the labor strike. The report stated that since the invasion of Shanghai by the Japanese, the silk merchants had taken the opportunity to increase working hours from eleven to twelve hours and reduce wages for male and female workers by 50-60%. The wages of female workers were reduced from 58 cents to 42 cents. All existing benefits, such as overtime subsidies for male workers and rewards for female workers, were canceled. Workers were also forced to prioritize increased output over quality, causing great suffering. The union repeatedly received reports from workers requesting a fair fight. The union immediately contacted the trade association to negotiate based on the situation. Initially, the factory owners used the excuse of the Japanese army not having withdrawn to delay. After the Chinese police took over, the union actively negotiated with the factory owners. On June 25th, a reply was received from the trade association, stating that working hours and careful production had been communicated to all factories and that the wage issue would be discussed at a meeting next week (this week) before a reply would be given. After receiving the reply, the union planned to continue negotiations. However, workers at the Yichang Silk Factory, possibly under the instigation of reactionary elements, acted impatiently and went on strike on the afternoon of June 25th. After receiving the news, the union immediately negotiated seriously with the factory owners in order to achieve the goal of freeing our workers from suffering. Therefore, the details of the strike are reported in writing, hoping for your review and guidance.

Meetings Between the Two Sides: The labor union convened a joint meeting of group leaders and staff members at 2:00 PM yesterday to discuss ways to resolve the labor strike. The decisions were: (1) Send representatives to petition party and government agencies. (2) Negotiate seriously with the factory owners to quickly resolve the labor strike. (3) Workers should wait patiently for a resolution and refrain from taking rash actions or creating trouble. (4) Closely prevent reactionary elements from taking the opportunity to cause chaos. At the same time, the factory owners also held a meeting at 1:00 PM at the Hujiamuqiao Fire Station, chaired by Zhang Peishen. After exchanging views, they decided to submit the issues of resumption of work and resolution of the labor strike to the Silk Industry Trade Association's general meeting to be held today for discussion.

Central Government Investigation: Jiang Hao, a special commissioner of the Central People's Movement Steering Committee, received instructions from the Central Government to investigate the truth about the silk factory labor strike. Jiang visited the union on Tiantong Road at 2:00 PM yesterday and met with Chen Xiupu, a director of the union, to inquire in detail about the causes of the strike, as well as treatment and working conditions. Jiang has submitted the results of the investigation to the Central Government for further instructions.

Hope for the Resolution of the Traditional Chinese Medicine Industry Labor Strike 178

Good Results from Yesterday's Negotiations

Peaceful Resolution Expected Soon

According to Dagong News Agency, the pharmaceutical industry workers in the city, due to their opposition to the management's refusal to use substitute workers, have caused a serious dispute. Yesterday, the labor representatives negotiated with the trade association. The negotiation results were quite satisfactory, and a resolution is expected soon. The details are recorded separately below.

Negotiation Situation: At 2:00 PM yesterday, the Salary Increase Movement Committee sent Zhao Zhenhui, Fang Qinghe, Feng Xingkang, Chen Yantao, Zhu Xiaqing, and other five people to the Traditional Chinese Medicine Trade Association to negotiate. Zhang Meian, a representative of the association, met with them. The labor representatives put forward three demands: (1) The original contract remains valid, and the management shall not arbitrarily breach it (and reported the breaches by various pharmacies). (2) Each person receives a monthly salary increase of ten yuan. (3) Placement of unemployed workers. Mr. Zhang expressed his acceptance of the principles of the three demands put forward by the labor representatives with the utmost sincerity, but they need to be submitted to the meeting for discussion and a formal reply can be given within three days. Finally, it was decided that labor and management would jointly form a joint committee to discuss salary increases, placement of unemployed workers, and other unfulfilled contract issues in order to seek a resolution so as not to expand the strike and achieve a peaceful resolution, so as not to cause panic among patients and put society in a state of unease. At that time, the negotiations between the two sides were very close, and the strike is expected to be resolved.

Workers' Declaration: All outfield workers in the traditional Chinese medicine industry issued an important declaration yesterday in opposition to joining the trade association. To all workers and people from all walks of life across the country: Since the establishment of the Pharmaceutical Friendship Association in the ninth year of the Republic of China under the warlord railways, although it has undergone several reorganizations with the change of environment, the entire organization has never had any shortcomings. Unexpectedly, recently, the management of our industry, because they could not arbitrarily oppress us, actually fantasized about falsely accusing our outfield workers of having no skills and being completely commercial employees. They should join the traditional Chinese medicine trade association, which has no membership qualifications in the municipal chamber of commerce, so as to divide our organization and follow their destructive plot. It must be known that our industry's workers have no internal or external distinction. The initial learning period requires three years. After completing their studies, they must practice for one or two years before choosing to work inside or outside according to their own preferences. Whether or not they have skills is very clear. Moreover, the same worker who is an outfield worker in one store is an infield worker in another store, which is very common. The facts are all there, so how can they be erased? Even if we consider it according to legal principles, freedom of assembly and association is absolutely guaranteed and is recorded in the provisional constitution. Moreover, there is a signing of the entire labor-management conditions. How can the trade association of the traditional Chinese medicine industry threaten and lure us, forcing us to join, disregarding national laws and labor-management conditions, and acting recklessly in a way that blinds them with greed? For the sake of their own interests and to preserve their dignity, we unanimously vow not to join. We will not count any sacrifices. In addition to requesting the labor union to fight for justice, we fear that workers and people from all walks of life across the country may not understand the truth, so we have briefly explained the situation. We hope that you will review and uphold justice, which will not only be a fortune for our colleagues, but also a fortune for workers across the country. This is our declaration.

Letter to the Labor Union: The Traditional Chinese Medicine Trade Association sent a letter to the Labor Union, stating: In reply, we have read the letter you sent. We found that the labor-management conditions of this association were signed in the spring of the sixteenth year of the Republic of China. At that time, the National Revolutionary Army had just reached Jiangnan, and the Kuomintang had not yet purged Shanghai. In this chaotic period, the temporary labor-management contract was originally intended to take into account the overall situation and support the revolution. After the National Government established its capital in Nanjing and the five branches were established at the same time, various industrial and commercial laws and regulations were promulgated in order. All private agreements concluded in the revolutionary process that are contrary to current laws should be amended in accordance with the law. The reason why the central government ordered this industry to amend the conditions last year was for this reason. Moreover, the contents of the labor-management conditions of this industry do not contain the words "permanent implementation." Therefore, if both parties feel that there are obstacles and terminate the conditions privately, they can still do so even without an order from the central government. If it is said that the existing contract cannot be changed, then this association's salary increase plan has already been recorded in the conditions, but your association does not abide by it and has plans to propose a salary increase. How can this be so contradictory? The minutes of the meeting disclosed by this association in various newspapers on the 16th of this month concerned the division of internal and external workers and the free recruitment of substitute workers. The former was in accordance with the instructions of the Central Training Committee, and the latter was in accordance with the instructions of the Bureau of Social Affairs. Neither has anything to do with this association's labor-management conditions. The newspapers are all there and can be checked. The letter stated that this association had completely destroyed the labor-management conditions without leaving any trace. What is the basis for saying that? As for the words "responsible personnel of your association have repeatedly advised us, but it is difficult to take effect," since the incident, this association has not met with any of your association's members. This kind of embellishment has no value in arguing. However, at this time of hot summer and abundant money, with severe epidemics, if your association instigates a strike because your demands are not met, brazenly disregarding the health of the people and society, then all the responsibilities will be borne by your association. This association does not dare to take credit for other people's achievements. This is a special reply to show a warning. We hope you will reflect on it. This is our earnest hope. Addressed to the Shanghai Municipal Traditional Chinese Medicine Industry Workers' Union.

Reply to the Warning: The Pharmaceutical Workers' Union sent a letter to Feng Cunrentang and other major pharmacies, issuing a warning. The Traditional Chinese Medicine Trade Association replied on their behalf, stating: We have received your association's warning and request to reply on behalf of our members, such as Feng Cunrentang. After investigating, we found that Feng Cunrentang and others refused to send outfield substitute workers in accordance with this association's notice and the instructions of the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, which is not inappropriate. Moreover, these pharmacies have always abided by the labor-management conditions set by this industry and have never destroyed them. The letter from your association is completely a false accusation. Furthermore, this time, this association's order to refuse outfield substitute workers is a city-wide issue, not a local issue for a few pharmacies. If your association has any negotiations, it should contact this association to handle them. The procedure for issuing a separate warning to these pharmacies lacks legality. This is a special reply to the previous letter. Please check and handle it accordingly. Addressed to the Pharmaceutical Industry Workers' Union.

Medical Association's Advice: The Shanghai National Medical Association, fearing that the pharmaceutical industry strike would harm the people's health, sent a letter of advice to both labor and management in the pharmaceutical industry, stating: Recently, we have read reports that the labor and management of your association have failed to reach an agreement, which is regrettable. It is summer, and diseases are rampant. The need for medicines is all the more urgent. We believe that your members understand the overall situation and will be able to work together in harmony to prevent the strike from escalating. This association has a close relationship with your association and is like brothers in the same boat. We cannot remain silent about this unfortunate event. In addition to sending a letter to the Traditional Chinese Medicine Industry Workers' Union, we especially request your association to consider the difficult times and prioritize the lives of the people, quickly resolve the issue peacefully, which would not only be a fortune for this association, but also a deep hope for all citizens.

Trade Association's Petition: The Traditional Chinese Medicine Trade Association, based on the resolution of the Emergency Executive Committee, sent Zhang Meian, Cen Zhiliang, Zhou Gansheng, and Feng Jinpu, four representatives, to various agencies this morning, including the Municipal Government, the Municipal Party Headquarters, the Bureau of Social Affairs, and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, to submit petitions.

Jiangsu Province Rice Association Telegraphed Request to Abolish Special Business Tax 180

A telegram was sent to the Jing authorities by the Jiangsu Ninghu City and County Rice Industry Association Federation regarding the special business tax levied by the Jiangsu Provincial Government. Yesterday, a telegram was sent to the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Finance, urging the abolition of the tax. The telegram stated that the special business tax levied by Jiangsu Province harms businesses and harms the people, even more so than the likin tax. Various trade associations have repeatedly appealed for relief. The Executive Yuan and the Ministry sympathized with the difficulties of businesses and ordered the abolition of the tax, which brought joy to the people. However, according to the members of the association, the Jiangsu Provincial Government is disregarding everything and still plans to establish offices and collect the tax starting on July 1st, allowing the government's credibility to be swept away, the people's livelihood to be destroyed, laws to be disregarded, and the hardships of businesses to be ignored, which is shocking. Although this association is based in the rice industry, most of the inland rice businesses also operate in soybeans and wheat. In reality, there is no distinction between primary and secondary. Moreover, soybeans and grains are both essential daily necessities. If heavy taxes are levied, they will be directly levied on businesses and indirectly taken from the common people. How can they bear this heavy tax after surviving the disaster? Even from the perspective of the system, Jiangsu Province is not a foreign land. How can it disregard the orders of the Executive Yuan and the Ministry? In order to respect national laws and take into account the difficulties of businesses and the people, the special business tax planned to be levied by Jiangsu Province cannot be allowed to be implemented freely. This association deeply feels the pain and cannot remain silent. We earnestly telegraph and request that the leaders review and instruct the Jiangsu Provincial Government to strictly abide by the express orders and quickly abolish the special business tax similar to the likin tax in order to respect the law and relieve the hardships of Jiangsu businesses. We are waiting for orders with the utmost urgency. Ye Huijun, Chairman of the Jiangsu Ninghu City and County Rice Industry Association Federation.

Therefore, there is no need to issue another protection order. Regarding the case of Anhui Province's harsh egg tax collection, this Ministry has already instructed the Anhui Finance Department to adhere to the approved business tax rates and to abolish the egg tax bureau. You are hereby notified."
