Cotton Association's Petition to Stop Borrowing American Cotton 183

The Chinese Cotton Industry Association presented a document to the central government, stating: "Petition Regarding the Nation-Damaging and People-Harming Issue of Borrowing American Cotton – Requesting Your Consideration and Intervention to Prevent This, for the Sake of National Stability and the Benefit of the People." We have read in the Nanjing Political News of the 24th of this month that Rong Zongjing, a prominent Shanghai flour and cotton merchant, recently borrowed 400,000 bales of American cotton at a weekly interest rate of 4%, to be repaid over four years, guaranteed by the government, and that Finance Minister Song is planning to submit this for approval at the Central Political Council meeting. The government authorities reportedly view this matter as having a significant impact on the domestic cotton industry and are mostly in favor of proceeding with caution. Upon reading this, the general sentiment is one of alarm. We believe that under the current circumstances, given the severe decline in our country's agricultural products, there are several reasons why borrowing American cotton is absolutely unacceptable. We respectfully present these to your ministries and departments. Our country is based on agriculture, and agricultural products, particularly silk, tea, cotton, and grain, have traditionally been the most important. Among these, the exports of silk and tea are substantial, generating significant annual revenue. However, due to the influx of foreign goods, the prices of silk and tea have plummeted. This year, there have been particularly large imports of Japanese silk, to the point where Chinese silk has no place to stand, leading to widespread closures. The underlying reason is undoubtedly the pressure from foreign goods. This is the first reason, based on silk and tea, why American cotton should not be borrowed. Our country produces many varieties of cotton, and the yield is considerable. If the harvest is at or above average, the domestically produced cotton should be sufficient to supply the domestic textile industry. In the past, the import of foreign cotton was limited, generally not exceeding 500,000 to 800,000 dan. After last year's floods, the harvest of Chinese cotton decreased, and foreign cotton flowed in continuously. From last autumn to the present, imports have reached 5 million dan, a truly alarming quantity. Furthermore, the existing stock of Chinese cotton in North and South China is still over 1 million dan, and the price per dan is 300-400 liang lower than that of foreign cotton. If we borrow another 1.5 million dan of foreign cotton, how will our existing stock of cotton be sold? This is the second reason, based on the existing stock of cotton, why American cotton should not be borrowed. Cotton farmers in our country account for at least one-tenth of the entire population. These cotton farmers, with their families, rely on the annual income from cotton production for their livelihood. Recently, due to the import of foreign cotton, prices have already fallen by more than 10 liang compared to last year, and even compared to foreign cotton, the price is 300-400 liang lower. If we borrow more foreign cotton, the price of Chinese cotton will fall further, and those who previously relied on it for their livelihood will have no means of survival. Driven by hunger and cold, the old and weak will perish, and the strong will resort to desperate measures. There is no greater hidden danger for the nation. This is the third reason, based on the people's livelihood, why American cotton should not be borrowed. The more foreign cotton is imported, the greater the outflow of cash. In our country, which is currently facing a financial crisis, such a large outflow of cash will deplete our financial lifeblood, leading to imminent collapse. How can social order be maintained? This is the fourth reason, based on social concerns, why American cotton should not be borrowed. Furthermore, the oversupply of American cotton has been widely discussed both domestically and internationally. The American government, in order to maintain the livelihoods of cotton farmers and businesses, is using the surplus cotton to achieve the reputation of lending while enjoying the benefits of increased sales. The merchants borrowing American cotton are considering the interests of American cotton farmers and businesses. Shouldn't they be considering the interests of our country's farmers and businesses? To abandon the root and pursue the branch is the ultimate folly. This is the fifth reason, based on the overall situation, why American cotton should not be borrowed. In conclusion, Chinese cotton is a major agricultural product, and the cotton industry is the source of livelihood for farmers and businesses. It is of utmost importance to both the national economy and the people's livelihood. As an association engaged in the cotton industry, we are familiar with the situation. Therefore, we dare to present this petition to your ministries and departments, hoping that you will consider the people's difficulties, promptly intervene, and firmly reject this proposal in order to strengthen the nation's foundation and benefit the people's livelihood. This is our urgent plea, and we respectfully request your consideration."

Russian Citizen Gletzky's Disappearance Case 184

The Shanghai Evening Post reports that Gletzky, a Russian proofreader at the Shanghai Russian-language newspaper Volimia, was arrested on the night of June 16th for disorderly conduct in the French Concession, along with three other Russian companions. The next day, they were sent to the Second Special District Court on Rue Chévaslier for trial, where Gletzky was sentenced to seven days in prison. On June 23rd, the other three Russians were released and went to Gletzky's residence at 108 Hua Long Road to inform his brother that Gletzky had disappeared. They said they had last seen him around 10 a.m. on the 19th. Two of them even claimed to have seen Gletzky bleeding, apparently from a blow to the chest, allegedly because Gletzky repeatedly asked for water, which angered the prison guards. Another heard Gletzky calling for help, followed by angry voices from the guards. Gletzky then reportedly claimed to be ill and requested to be sent to a hospital for treatment. After that, Gletzky reportedly disappeared. Upon hearing this, Gletzky's brother went to the prison to demand his brother's body, but the prison guards claimed to know nothing. Gletzky's brother then reported the matter to Mr. Meizige, the chairman of the Russian Emigrant Association. Mr. Meizige has sent a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Government authorities inquiring about the matter. Upon hearing the news, the French police have reportedly reported the matter to the French Consulate General and are conducting a thorough investigation. This morning, the French police claimed that if evidence is found, the French Concession authorities plan to protest to the Chinese authorities.

Little Luzon Hat Cleaning Shop Sues for Trademark Infringement 185

Sun Pianshi, manager of Little Luzon Hat Cleaning Shop, recently hired lawyers Chen Zhongyin and Ye Fukang to sue Lu Rongde, manager of Meili Na Hat Cleaning Shop on Sima Road, in the First Special District Court for using a similar trademark, requesting the court to stop the infringement. The grounds for the lawsuit are as follows: "Little Luzon" is the popular name for the capital of the Philippine Islands, its English name being Manila. The plaintiff registered the name "Little Luzon" with the National Trademark Bureau of the National Government. The defendant also translated the English name of the capital into Chinese as "Meili Na". According to Article 19 of the Effective Business Practices, in the same city or town, others are not allowed to imitate a registered business name to engage in the same business. Article 20 states that if a registered business name is imitated by others or a similar business name is used for unfair competition, the merchant of the original business name may petition to prohibit its use and request compensation for damages. The defendant's use of the plaintiff's name in the same city or town is obviously illegal, and therefore a lawsuit is filed to stop the infringement. In addition to imitating the plaintiff's business name, the defendant also uses the trademark "Little Luzon Method". After the plaintiff discovered this, they applied to the Trademark Bureau for identification. They have now received identification letter No. 99, which recognizes that there is a suspicion of counterfeiting. "Little Luzon" is the name of the plaintiff's business name and trademark. There is no special hat cleaning method, commercially or chemically, called the "Little Luzon Method". Therefore, it is a deliberate infringement. According to Article 14 of the Trademark Law, the plaintiff is entitled to request a prohibition of its use. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Su opened a court session for questioning. Yuan Yangan and Ma Yizhong, lawyers for Meili Na, argued that the plaintiff only registered the business name "Little Luzon Hat Shop" and cannot claim ownership of the name "Little Luzon" itself. For example, Shen Bao has never sued to prohibit the publication of newspapers such as "Shanghai," "Hu," and "Xin Shen" simply because the newspaper is named after "Shen," a place name. Similarly, regarding Jinling Restaurant versus Nanjing Restaurant, and West Lake Hotel versus Lakeside Hotel, if there is no identical or similar wording on the face of it, how can it be considered infringement? Furthermore, the defendant is also registered and has provided detailed rebuttals regarding trademark matters. The court ordered that the hearing be adjourned to another date.

Recreation and Entertainment Activities Held at War Zone Orphanage 188

Farewell to Mrs. Simpson. Yesterday afternoon, starting at 4:00 PM, the Shanghai War Zone Orphanage held recreation and entertainment activities to bid farewell to Mrs. Simpson. The details are as follows:

Attendees: Those present yesterday included Mr. and Mrs. Simpson, General Zhu Ziqiao, Shen Junwen, Xu Rufa, Xu Jigang, Yang Shuping, Sun Fuzhang, Fang Chongde, Qian Zhesheng, Mrs. Bonard, Mrs. Bao Chuanxian, Mrs. Mason, Mrs. He Chenger, Mrs. Byler, Ms. Ma Mulan, Ms. Xu Xiuzhen, Ms. Wu Yuxun, Ms. Hu Zhou Shuan, Ms. Zhou Shujing, Luo Yunyan, Vice President of the Compassionate Infants Association, Wu Weide, Director General, Chen Tiesheng, Deputy Director General, Chen Zhengfan, Zhang Yueru, Xuan Bokun, Ms. Xu Yunru, Mrs. Zhang Xuelou, Director of the Orphanage, staff members Huang Zhenyong, He Yuren, Ms. Zhu Hanwen, Ms. Gong Xiyin, Xu Yong, He Yuren, Ms. Zhu Hanwen, Ms. Gong Xiyin, Ms. Xu Baozhen, and over 100 other people, plus participating children, totaling over 500 people.

Exhibition of Achievements: The War Zone Orphanage has been established for nearly five months. The operation is quite well-managed. For this recreation and entertainment event, a special room was set aside to display student achievements, which were dazzling and delightful. It is said that the various works were all designed by Ms. Zhu Hanwen, a female teacher at the orphanage.

Then, Boy Scout representative He Guibin gave a thank you speech, expressing sincere acceptance.

When the war broke out in Shanghai, he spoke out righteously, strongly condemning the Japanese military's indiscriminate bombing. Mrs. Simpson is kind and benevolent, sparing no effort in protecting war-zone children. Since the establishment of this orphanage, we have received much assistance from them. It can be seen that Mr. and Mrs. Simpson have come from a thousand miles away, and what they have left for us is only benevolence and righteousness. Today, we bid farewell to Mr. and Mrs. Simpson as they return to their country, and we hope that they will be able to return to this land as soon as possible to benefit this country. We are extremely fortunate."

Mr. and Mrs. Simpson are doing their best to seek happiness for the Chinese people, making us feel that we met them too late. We hope that China's foundation can be consolidated as soon as possible and enter the realm of prosperity and strength. We also hope that the children here today will all strive to make progress, set lofty goals, and become healthy citizens in the future, serving the country and serving humanity."

Student Speech: Finally, Yang Huiming, a student representative from the orphanage, gave a farewell speech to Mrs. Simpson, saying: "We will remember the favors we have received from Mrs. Simpson in our hearts and never forget them. We have lost our parents and families today because of the crimes of Japanese imperialism. We must set our goals to fight for the liberation and freedom of the Chinese nation, and use Mrs. Simpson's great love to help other oppressed small nations." The entire audience applauded continuously. Afterwards, Chinese and foreign photographers came to take pictures, and then the meeting was adjourned. It was already 6:30 PM.

Lu Lanchun Sued 190

Biological Father Sues Her for Neglecting Support

Lu Countersues, Denying Father-Daughter Relationship

Court Hearing Today Afternoon

Kunqu actress Lu Lanchun, who was once famous in the opera world and highly regarded in the performing arts, disappeared from the stage after marrying Xue YanSheng, the second son of wealthy merchant Xue BaoRong. Recently, her biological father Yu WeiWen (号致案) came from his hometown of Yancheng to Shanghai and hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit in the First Special District Court for abandonment, claiming that when Lu Lanchun was seven years old, after her mother Zhu was divorced, she was sent to a Chen to learn opera. Later, Zhu took her away and she was subjected to abuse by Zhu and her lover Zhang DaMianzi. Zhang even forced her to be a concubine. The plaintiff traveled to Shanghai and Hankou and provided financial assistance to rescue her. Grateful, the defendant acknowledged that she would support the plaintiff for the rest of his life. Now that the defendant has married the wealthy merchant Xue Yansheng and has abundant food and clothing, the plaintiff has repeatedly contacted the defendant through intermediaries to fulfill the promise of support, but the defendant, with a hardened heart, has resolutely refused. According to Article 310 of the Criminal Law, a person who abandons someone with no ability to support themselves, whom they are legally or contractually obligated to assist, nurture, or protect, or who fails to provide necessary assistance, nurture, or protection for their survival, should be held criminally liable. The plaintiff is in his declining years, impoverished and ill, alone and without any support, and his plight is unbearable. Therefore, he has filed a lawsuit according to law, requesting that the defendant be punished accordingly, and incidentally

Requests Reservation of Civil Suit. Upon receiving the complaint, the court immediately issued a summons, notifying the defendant Lu Lanchun to respond according to law. Lu also hired lawyers Wang Fuchang and Wu Linkun to submit a statement to the court, in addition to defending herself and filing a countersuit. Her defense is divided into two points: (1) Procedure: Yu Zhicai once filed a similar lawsuit in the 20th year of the Republic of China (1931), suing Lu for abandonment, which was dismissed by the court. Now, Yu Zhicai has suddenly become Yu Weiwen, first claiming to be her biological father, and then claiming to be her foster parent, constantly litigating, only hoping to defraud her of money. Based on the principle that a criminal case cannot be tried twice, the lawsuit should be dismissed. (2) Substance: The plaintiff is neither Lu's biological father nor her foster parent, and he has

Sold Lu Repeatedly. The relationship of gratitude and obligation was severed long ago. As early as the 8th year of the Republic of China (1919), the plaintiff had civil lawsuits filed in the Jiangsu Local Court, the Jiangsu High Court, and the Beijing Dali Yuan, all of which resulted in judgments on record. Upon review of the above judgments, not only is there no parental relationship between the defendant and the plaintiff, but she was sold repeatedly, severing all ties of gratitude and obligation long ago. Therefore, there is no obligation to support her, and the crime of abandonment cannot be established. Previously, when Lu was singing opera, her income was substantial. Now that she has married into the Xue family,

He is Driven by Greed. He has been involved in criminal and civil litigation, causing endless entanglement. However, the defendant's loss of reputation and suffering are unspeakable. Therefore, the lawsuit should be dismissed. As for the reasons for the countersuit, they are based on Article 180 of the Criminal Law, which states that anyone who intends to subject another person to criminal or disciplinary punishment and falsely accuses them to the relevant public official shall be sentenced to imprisonment for a term of not more than seven years, and Article 363, which states that anyone who intends to illegally possess property belonging to themselves or a third party and uses fraudulent means to cause a person to deliver property belonging to themselves or a third party shall be sentenced to imprisonment for a term of not more than five years, or detention, and may also be fined or have their fine commuted for an amount not exceeding 1,000 yuan. Yu has no parental relationship with Lu and has repeatedly sold her, and Lu has no obligation to support him. However, he disregards the reputation of others, repeatedly resorts to criminal charges, and publishes them in newspapers, hoping to defraud her of money. Therefore, he is undoubtedly guilty of false accusation and attempted fraud.

A Countersuit is Filed According to Law. Requesting punishment to warn against evil and protect the good. The case was originally scheduled to be heard yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, with Judge Wu Tingqi specially opening a criminal court. Therefore, Yu Weiwen arrived on time and sat in a corner waiting for the hearing. Yu, who is nearly 60 years old, was wearing a blue cloth gown yesterday, looking like someone from the countryside. Lu Lanchun did not appear in court. Judge Wu ascended the bench at 1:30 PM and first heard a theft case, but the hearing did not conclude until 3:30 PM. Realizing that the Lu case could not be heard, he informed the lawyers of both parties to reschedule the hearing for 2:30 PM this afternoon (the 29th). This caused the general public to make a wasted trip. With the hearing being held today, Shanghai residents, impressed by Lu's fame, will likely flock to the court to listen in.

Yesterday Morning's Assassination on Min Guo Road 191

Cao Akun Had Enmity with Others

Thugs Broke in and Fired Three Shots

Cao Requested an Emergency Injection

His Wife Arrived Only to Find Him Dead

Cao Akun, a 31-year-old man from Jiangyin living at No. 50 Renji Road, Pudong, used to work as a foreman at the wharves along the Bund in the French Concession. In reality, he specialized in insurance and transporting contraband. He had many followers, which led to him making enemies. Cao often went to the Heliyuan Inn, a three-story building at No. 78 Min Guo Road outside the Xiaodongmen in the French Concession, to play cards in the Ruiji Zhuang room. The Heliyuan Inn was opened by a Ningbo native named Sang Dingsheng, nominally as a cargo storage facility, but in reality, it was a

Disguised Association, exclusively for gatherings and card games among dockworkers. Cao arrived at Ruiji Zhuang in Heliyuan around 5 or 6 PM the day before yesterday and played mahjong with Shen Hongquan, Zhu Ajin, and Wang Wangshi. His enemies found out and sent three thugs in plain clothes armed with weapons to wait outside Heliyuan,

Loitering in the Middle of the Road, waiting to attack Cao when he came out. Cao seemed to have sensed something while playing cards upstairs, so he dared not come downstairs until late at night, continuing to play mahjong until dawn, not ending the game. He intended to leave when the street was bustling with pedestrians, hoping to avoid trouble. Unexpectedly, the thugs waited until 5 AM this morning, and unable to wait any longer, the three rushed up to the third floor, straight to the Ruiji Zhuang room. Seeing Cao still playing cards, two guarded the door while one entered, calling Cao's name directly. When Cao responded, they

Opened Fire with a Handgun, firing three shots in succession. The bullets hit Cao's chest, with two penetrating and one lodged in his back. Cao fell wounded. Seeing their objective achieved, the assailants turned around and fled downstairs in a panic. The three who were playing cards with Cao were all terrified and ran to hide. Later, his companions and his girlfriend, Zhang Axiang, hired a car to take Cao to Renji Hospital for treatment. Upon hearing the news, the Xiaodongmen police immediately dispatched Chinese and foreign detectives to investigate the scene, recovering a bullet casing and inquiring about the appearance and clothing of the assailants, reporting back to the head detective for review. When Cao arrived at the hospital, he was still conscious and able to speak. After the doctor applied medicine and bandages, he still felt unbearable pain and requested

An Emergency Injection, wanting to wait for his wife to arrive to meet and talk, and to identify the number and names of the assailants. He also told his girlfriend, Zhang Axiang, that he knew his life was in danger and instructed Zhang to tell his wife to avenge him. At 5:50 AM, his wife, Mrs. Dai, heard the news at home and rushed to the hospital. Cao had already died of his injuries, and the couple did not get to meet. The hospital notified the Xiaodongmen police, who sent detectives to carry the body to the Tongren Fuyuan branch for an autopsy. At 10 AM, the criminal division of the General Police Department reported to Wu Xiaoke, the prosecutor of the Second Special Court, who, accompanied by a forensic doctor, arrived at the location to examine the body. After confirming the identity of the body, he took his seat in court. According to the report of the detective, Cao Dai, the wife of the deceased, claimed,

Her Husband was Tragically Murdered, requesting the arrest of the murderer and seeking justice. The official ordered that it be verified that Cao Akun had indeed died from gunshot wounds before his death. The body was handed over to his wife for funeral arrangements, pending the police's arrest of the murderer for investigation. After the examination, the police took photos of the body and had the family prepare a coffin for burial. Meanwhile, the police found out that the Heliyuan Inn, where the incident occurred, was operating without a license, violating the regulations of the工部局 (Municipal Council), and took the inn owner, Sang Dingsheng, into custody for further investigation. Since the occurrence of this case, the police department has dispatched Chinese and foreign detectives to search for the perpetrators, and it is reported that one person has been arrested and taken back to the police station for further investigation.

Further Trial of a Land Deed Dispute of Several Years 192

Redemption Money Paid, Land Deed Not Retrieved

Transfer of Ownership Not Clearly Stated

Supreme Court Deems All Suspicious

High Court Second Branch to Open Trial on the 9th

The financial circle of Shanghai is paying close attention to the land deed dispute between a large bank at No. 198 Dexin Lane, Nanjing Road, and the Spanish Church of Wangde Hall at No. 10 Yangshupu Road. The case has been in litigation for several years and has now been sent back for retrial by the Supreme Court. Initially, in 1927, the large bank received a mortgage on a piece of land located on Avenue Joffre under the name of Zhang Zuyong. At that time, Zhang provided not only the land deed but also various mortgage and sale contracts from owners such as the Oriental Bank. Wangde Hall claimed that these documents were later lost by the Oriental Bank when they were entrusted to transfer the ownership, and they had issued a public statement, etc. In the first trial, the large bank won the case. Wangde Hall appealed to the High Court Second Branch, which ruled that the large bank should return the land deed and other documents to Wangde Hall. The large bank then hired lawyer Ma Junshuo to appeal to the Supreme Court, which resulted in a ruling to send the case back for retrial. The reasons for the ruling were roughly as follows: "The matter that should be investigated in this case is whether the disputed English land deed No. 11199 has been redeemed by Wangde Hall. Reviewing the records, the land deed was mortgaged by Tai Mi Qu Lei Adiesi to Kaden on September 27, 1922, and then transferred by Kaden to the Oriental Bank. The term expired on September 27, 1925, without redemption. According to the agreement, the Oriental Bank mortgaged it to Zhang Zuyong as collateral. Therefore, it is difficult to say that Zhang's acceptance of the mortgage was invalid. Although Wangde Hall claimed to have paid off the mortgage debt for redemption, if it had indeed redeemed the mortgage, it should have retrieved all the mortgage documents as proof of the extinction of the mortgage right. Why allow them to remain in the hands of the large bank, and even not reclaim the land deed? This is even more incomprehensible. If they entrusted the Oriental Bank to transfer the ownership, the Oriental Bank should have indicated 'transfer of ownership on behalf' in the receipt after receiving the land deed. Why is there not a single word? All of these are suspicious. If a detailed investigation is conducted, the truth can be easily obtained. As to whether the large bank has an obligation to return the land deed, it should be determined by whether Wangde Hall can definitively prove that Zhang Zuyong had not mortgaged the land to the Oriental Bank before he redeemed it." The case is now scheduled to open trial on August 9. Liu Hongyuan, the manager of the large bank, has submitted a petition to the High Court Second Branch, stating that in the Shanghai business community, mortgages are the key to financial turnover, and land deed mortgages are especially important. If there is a formal land deed, a proper mortgage document, and a transfer of ownership certificate, the procedure is complete. Therefore, he requests a judgment based on custom.

Dance Hall Girl Denies Her Fiancé from the Countryside 193

Fiancé Files a Lawsuit to Confirm the Marriage Contract

Wu Ailin, a 17-year-old dance hall girl at the Xin Xin Dance Hall, had her story of falling into the dance hall previously reported in the newspapers. Her fiancé, Wu Quangen, who works as a boatman, learned that Ailin had been lured to Shanghai by the wife of Chen Jinghua to work as a dance hall girl, so he also tracked her down, wanting to take her home. However, Ailin at this time had completely modernized and refused to acknowledge Quangen as her fiancé. Therefore, Quangen filed a petition with the civil mediation office of the First Special District Court, but mediation was unsuccessful. Now, he has gone a step further and filed a lawsuit against Ailin to confirm the marriage contract, requesting a judgment confirming that the marriage contract between the plaintiff and the defendant is legally established. Yesterday morning, Judge Yang of the First Special Court opened the court to summon them. The plaintiff, Wu Quangen, wearing short coarse clothes and cloth shoes, did not lose his rural character. The defendant, Wu Ailin, wearing a printed silk shirt, silk stockings, and leather shoes, with puffy short hair covering the back of her head, one rural and one fashionable, were worlds apart. A clumsy husband and a beautiful wife facing each other in court attracted even more attention. After Judge Yang took his seat, the plaintiff's lawyer, Fang Jiazhen, stated the case. Wu Quangen then

Detailed the reasons why he married the defendant as a child bride through his parents years ago, and then sent her to his aunt's house for upbringing. Unexpectedly, in May of last year, she was lured to Shanghai by a woman surnamed Chen to work as a dance hall girl. He also claimed that the defendant's real name was Hou Panmei, also known as Gendi. When questioned, Wu Ailin refused to acknowledge that the plaintiff was her fiancé. After debate by the lawyers of both parties, Judge Yang announced that the verdict would be announced at a later date.

Female Corpse in an Old Mat 195

Wound Near the Anus

Clearly Moved After Death

At 9:10 PM last night, a female corpse that had been discarded was suddenly discovered near the back door of No. 16, Lane 1, Fukang Lane, Avenue LaFayette, in the French Concession. The deceased was around 20 years old, short in stature, with short, disheveled hair, and a gold tooth in her upper right jaw. She was naked from the waist up, with only a pair of red willow-striped foreign cloth short pants on her lower body, barefoot and without shoes. The body was wrapped in a foreign cloth single mattress and an old mat. When passersby discovered it, they initially suspected it was a beggar curled up there. Upon closer inspection, the head and feet were not visible at both ends of the mat, and they kicked it repeatedly without movement, arousing suspicion. They then notified the lane manager to inspect it together. Upon unfolding the mattress and mat, a naked female corpse was revealed. They immediately reported it to the police, who rushed to investigate. There were no wounds on the body, but upon close inspection, it was clear that the body had been moved there after death. The Tongren Fuyuan branch was notified to dispatch a coffin bearer to carry the body to the autopsy center, pending a report to the Second Special District Court for examination. However, after the body was taken to the autopsy center and examined again, a wound was found near the anus. The police are currently investigating whether she was murdered.

Science

Homemade Small Desk Lamp 211

— Qing

The desk lamps sold in the market are mostly large, and the electricity they consume is also quite considerable. We find them somewhat uneconomical. Now there's a method to make a small desk lamp yourself. Not only does it save electricity, but it's also very interesting. Its brightness is sufficient for desk use. Readers may want to try it. The method is as follows: (Materials) A square transformer (commonly used for doorbells, which can convert ordinary voltage into 3-1/2 volts), one

A small light bulb (around 6V, commonly known as a car bulb), one

A small lamp holder (for inserting the small light bulb), one. Insulated wire (length determined by the distance from the power source), one length

Cloth-covered wire (about 2 feet of size 20), one length. A cigar box made of wood (approximately 5 inches in length, width, and height), one

A small wooden board (approximately 4 and 6/7 inches square), one piece. Male and female plugs, two each

(Of the above items, apart from the wooden box and board, the rest are sold in large electrical supply stores. Sometimes they are also sold at used goods stalls, and the prices are much cheaper than new ones, but broken ones are unusable.)

(Assembly) Connect both ends of one end of the insulated wire to both ends of one end of the transformer. Connect two pieces of cloth-covered wire to both ends of the other end of the transformer. Then nail the transformer onto the board, put it in the box, and nail it down. Make a hole in the side of the box for the insulated wire to pass through. Make two more holes on the other side, each with a female plug installed. Connect the two ends of the two cloth-covered wires from one end of the transformer to these two female plugs. Then take two more cloth-covered wires, connect one end to the lamp holder, and the other end to the male plugs. Then install the light bulb into the lamp holder. Once this is assembled, connect the other end of the insulated wire to a power source (i.e., ordinary AC power, about 200V). When in use, plug the male and female plugs together, and the light will turn on! However, one thing to note is whether the voltage output from the transformer matches the voltage required by the light bulb. If it's too low, the light won't turn on. If it's too high, it will easily burn out the filament. To avoid this issue, it's best to buy a rheostat and install it in between. Connect one end of the rheostat to one end of the transformer, and the other end to one of the female plugs. When in use, simply slowly turn the rheostat, and the light will gradually brighten. However, don't turn it too far, just until it's bright enough, otherwise, you will burn out the filament. Turning it backward will gradually dim it. Turning it all the way to the end will turn it off. It's like a kerosene lamp, where you can freely adjust the brightness and turn it off, and the filament is not easily burned out, making it much more interesting than a large desk lamp!

The above are the main principles of installation and connection. As for the exterior decoration, readers can think for themselves. You can decorate it however you like as long as you follow these principles!

Student

Old Li's Diary 212

— Fojin

Today in English class, the bell had rung a long time ago, but our female teacher still hadn't arrived, and the students were getting a little impatient.

"Old Li," classmate Zhou covered his mouth with his hand, leaned close to my ear, and said in a very small voice, "I'm afraid Ms. Huang has her 'monthly red' again, otherwise why isn't she here yet?"

"Not necessarily, maybe she has something else," I said with a smile.

Indeed, our female English teacher really gives the students too much to talk about. If she takes leave for an hour or is late by five or six minutes, the naughty students take the opportunity to say inappropriate things. Some say rude things like classmate Zhou, while others say she went to find a lover. One person says one thing, another says another, gossiping and saying the most awful things. The male students burst out laughing when they hear it, while the female students blush. But these naughty students say whatever comes to mind, and you really can't stop them.

However, Ms. Huang really does give the students something to talk about. Although she is in her thirties, her face is still painted red, and she changes her cheongsam every time she comes. According to my calculations, she has taught for four weeks, three hours each week, and she has changed twelve cheongsams in total. It's like a bride changing wedding dresses, truly "old in years but young at heart."

However, Ms. Huang teaches English very well, explaining each word and sentence clearly, and her pronunciation is also very accurate. Because of this, many students are very eager to attend her class, and very few are absent without reason. Even students from other classes come to freeload and join in the fun. This is a problem because after the "January 28th Incident," when the Sino-Japanese war in Shanghai broke out, most of the university campuses were turned into ashes by Japanese imperialism. Therefore, this semester, all the universities tucked their tails between their legs and ran to the concession to rent foreign houses to start school. The foreign houses rented by C University, although there are more than a dozen classrooms, are narrow and small, so the students have to fight for chairs when class starts and ends, like refugees抢米 (抢米 means to grab rice), the weaker female students are squeezed into the corners by the male students, and they can only watch helplessly. Therefore, the female students come very early to English class, especially today, because when the previous class ended, Ms. Huang told us that she would be asking questions today. Not only did the female students come very early, but the male students also came very early.

The students were still sitting and waiting. Five minutes, ten minutes, a quarter of an hour passed, and Ms. Huang still hadn't arrived.

"Old Li, isn't it: I guessed right with just one sentence." When the students dispersed and walked out of the classroom door, classmate Zhou patted me on the shoulder and asked me in a very funny tone.

"Not necessarily, maybe she has something else," I still said.

Complexion Problem

A Woman 213

— Wenbai

The poorer the society, the more fraudulent and deceitful activities there are. This is a natural and immutable causal relationship. Unfortunately, being born in China today as a commoner with no livelihood security means you often face the danger of unemployment. Once unemployed, there is no food to eat, no clothes to wear, and no house to live in. So, the more honest ones beg, and the more mischievous ones become thieves. Aren't we already tired of seeing theft cases in the daily newspapers? And those kinds of fraudulent things, the big ones are also seen in the daily newspapers, and the smaller ones, as long as you often stroll around the crossroads, you can't avoid encountering them repeatedly. Like selling fake rings, fake jewelry: etc., are things that everyone already knows, but the trick of the woman I saw that day was new ｜｜ at least it was the first time I discovered it.

The matter is like this: that day, I went to get a haircut with a friend, and when we passed by Stealing Chicken Bridge, a woman wearing a willow branch short shirt suddenly came to ask for directions:

"Excuse me, sir! How do I get to Gaochang Temple from here?" she said.

"From here, take the Route 5 tram to Ximen; at Ximen, transfer to another tram and you can go directly to Gaochang Temple," my friend told her.

"No, I'm asking how to walk there?"

"Walk there? There are many ways to go. You should take the tram!" my friend said, seeing that she was not a very healthy woman.

"But sir, I don't have a single copper coin on me. How can I take the tram! Can you do a good deed, sir, and give me two dimes? I would be grateful to you even in death!" She suddenly revealed a look of sorrow, and tears seemed about to fall.

Seeing this, you really couldn't bear it, so my compassionate friend generously gave her two dimes. After thanking us repeatedly, we went our own way.

Not long after, when we came back from the haircut and passed by the original place, we saw that the woman wearing the willow branch short shirt was still at the entrance of the mosque on Stealing Chicken Bridge, and there was a merchant-like man giving her money. When we saw this, we knew she was a swindler, and we immediately wanted to confront her, but when she saw us, she fled in a puff of smoke. What could we do?

Maidens and Toys 214

— Songlu

According to a report from the Electric Communication Society, there is a record as follows:

"The delegation of maidens from Manchukuo, Lei Jingshu, Yang Yun, Tsuda Sumiko, Toizumi Yukiko, Kim Kunwon, etc., arrived in Tokyo at 8 PM last night. This morning, they went to Nijubashi Bridge to pay their respects remotely to the Imperial Palace, and then visited Meiji Jingu Shrine and Yasukuni Shrine. At 11 AM, they met Mayor Taida and delivered the official documents of Manchukuo. At 1 PM, they attended a welcome meeting held by Tokyo City at Hibiya Hall, where Tokyo City presented them with dolls as toys."

"Women are toys?" This saying has long been scorned by the ladies and gentlemen of our Republic of China, and they have obtained equal rights for men and women from the government. Unexpectedly, these maidens from Manchukuo are actually willing to lower themselves and beg for pity from Japanese imperialists, to pay their respects remotely to the Imperial Palace, and to accept the toys given by Tokyo City. This puppet comedy, which is both comical and heartbreaking, is so sad, shameful, lamentable, and laughable!

Originally, the so-called government of Manchukuo was a puppet organization under Japanese violence, and these maiden envoys are puppets under puppets! The so-called rulers of Manchukuo are originally toys in the hands of the Japanese, and this group of maiden envoys are merely toys of the toy players, offering gifts indirectly and then directly. This magic lantern-style old trick has long been exposed by countries all over the world. We are just pitiful children, knowing that we have been coerced and deceived by the performers, but we dare not utter a word to them.

Some say: How can these maiden envoys willingly act as playthings? They are just like the children hired by Shandong street performers, forced to do so by violence! I say: Poor them! Poor these maidens, not only have their bodies been raped by the Japanese, but their pure hearts have also been raped by the Japanese! Besides pitying them, we can only blame our family head for being weak, so that our wives and daughters are offered for the trampling of foreign races! Alas! How painful!

Needle Pricks 215

— Yan Meng

｜China and Japan｜

Chinese people talk but don't do｜

Japanese people do but don't talk.

X X X X X

Chinese politicians strive to sing high-pitched tunes, trying to see who dreams of entering heaven.

Japanese politicians bury themselves in practical work, testing to see who is truly willing to enter hell.

X X X X X

Chinese tour groups go sightseeing everywhere, but in the end, they gain nothing except for the opportunity to flirt or travel and play. At most, they take a few landscape photos.

When Japanese observation groups go to a place, they always carefully deliberate and discuss how many resources there are, where they can colonize, and where they can open up new horizons.

X X X X X

Chinese people say that Japanese people are vicious, barbaric, selfish, and scheming. : : :

Japanese people laugh that Chinese people are clever, civilized, compassionate, and generous. : : :

X X X X X

Japanese science is progressing extremely rapidly,

The rapid progress of Chinese metaphysics is directly proportional.

X X X X X

The Japanese government feels that the Manchurian incident cannot fully satisfy public opinion,

At the same time, the Chinese government is quite comfortable with their effective governance of the people.

X X X X X

Japan uses guns and cannons,

China uses "verbal attacks and written condemnations."

X X X X X

The Japanese government is eager to try it out itself. The Chinese government is calmly waiting for the League of Nations to resolve it.

X X X X X

Japanese warlords point their guns outwards.

Chinese warlords point their guns inwards.

X X X X X

Japanese officials in power are unanimously studying how to deal with foreign affairs?

Chinese wealthy people are also scheming internally, seeing whose conditions are more favorable?

X X X X X

Japan dislikes the smallness of the island of Mishima and is determined to expand its colonies.

China fears that its territory is too wide and is trying its best to give away territory to others.

Market News 216

Library Sound Publication The China Library Sound is the only publication in the country that conveys the voices of the library community and researches library science. It is beautifully printed and full of content. The eighth issue will be published tomorrow. The content includes the relationship between family libraries and family education, my views on the further studies of librarians, practical book classification methods, encyclopedic reference materials, title categories, and the phenomenon of the postwar revival of Shanghai library services, etc. Each issue is five cents, and the annual subscription for twelve issues is five jiao. Exquisite library supplies are also given to subscribers. The general distribution point is the Minli Middle School Library in Dananmen, Shanghai.

Dai Shishi's Month of Reduced Fees Dai Shishi, the owner of the Jianyinglou in Yuanhu, has been living in Shanghai since he returned from his political career in Wuchen. He makes a living by painting, and his brushstrokes are as ethereal as clouds. He has long been respected by the art community. His style is deeply rooted in the quiet and serene brushwork of the Song dynasty. He is proficient in landscapes and figures, and he is especially skilled in flowers, birds, fish, and insects. He and the modern ink farmers Yao Sheng and others are in agreement but work in different ways. It is heard that Dai is holding a month of reduced fees from today onwards to broaden the connections of calligraphy and painting, calculated at 20% off as usual. The receiving address is No. 72 Sichuan Road and No. 1 Ruyili, Jinjiafang, Ximen. This city's major fan stores said.

Zhou Wenqing Provides Medical Care Zhou Wenqing from Yinshui has clinics at the Cunji Hospital on Sixth Ma Road and the Zhengfeng Medical Clinic on Fourth Ma Road, Yunnan Road. He specializes in treating venereal diseases and leukorrhea, using injection therapy with deep experience. Now, to facilitate the poor, he only charges two jiao for the registration fee in the morning.

Guangdetang Anniversary Discount The Guangdetang Chinese Medicine Shop on the west side of the Jiangning Guild Hall on Xinzha Road is holding its 30th-anniversary celebration this time. The prices are restrained, the selection of goods is conscientious, and there are valuable gifts, so customers from far and near are flocking to it. The family's treasured ginseng, Kejindan, epidemic prevention holy medicine Chunyang Jisheng Water, etc., are selling especially well. The anniversary period is scheduled to end on July 4th. Civil Judgments: ▲ Pingjinggu's lawsuit against Luo Zhifang for rent: The defendant shall pay the plaintiff rent of 2 yuan and 2 jiao; the plaintiff's other claims are dismissed; the defendant shall bear 9/10 of the litigation costs and the plaintiff shall bear 1/10. ▲ Xinkang Company's lawsuit against Zhang Boqin for rent arrears: The defendant shall repay the plaintiff 360 yuan in rent; the defendant shall bear the litigation costs. ▲ Wang Zhongliang's lawsuit against Song Along et al. for compensation: The defendants shall be jointly and severally liable for compensating the plaintiff for vegetable costs of 69 yuan, 5 jiao, 9 fen, and 2 li; the plaintiff's other claims are dismissed; the plaintiff shall bear 1/3 of the litigation costs and the defendants shall jointly and severally bear 2/3. ▲ Yuan Liansheng's lawsuit against Shao Amao et al. for rent arrears: The defendant Shao Amao shall repay the plaintiff 40 yuan in rent; Zhang Qingtang shall repay the plaintiff 32 yuan in rent; Wu Qichang shall repay the plaintiff 28 yuan in rent; and Du Yide shall repay the plaintiff 32 yuan in rent; each defendant shall bear the litigation costs in proportion. ▲ Zhu Yan's lawsuit against Zhu Hengjiang and the incidental civil lawsuit: The plaintiff's lawsuit is dismissed; the plaintiff shall bear the litigation costs.

Criminal Instructions: ▲ Wei Dehui's withdrawal of the petition is noted. Since this case falls under primary jurisdiction and the victim does not wish to punish Yu Jihai, the case should be dismissed. ▲ Xu Gengsheng's lawsuit against Song Jinquan for assault is noted. Since the case has already been prosecuted and judged, the request is deemed unnecessary. ▲ Li Wanguo et al.'s request for preventing false accusations is noted. If Ma Xiaolaohan et al. engage in extortion, the petitioners may report to the police station to handle the case. It is not necessary to file a preliminary record. The petitioners are informed accordingly. ▲ Fang Renxiao's lawsuit against Fang Zhoushi for theft is noted. If his wife has stolen items, he may report the facts in detail for investigation. It is not necessary to file a preliminary record. The petitioner is informed accordingly. ▲ Yang Changshan et al.'s petition for interrogation is noted. If the defendants have indeed committed criminal acts, the petitioners should report to the relevant public security bureau or district office to apprehend and hand them over to the court for interrogation and investigation. ▲ Yang Budeng's request for legal investigation is noted. Since the defendant Ma Deyuan has already died from illness, the subject of the crime has ceased to exist. The request is deemed unnecessary.

Civil Instructions: ▲ Dafeng Rice Store's Zhang Chongxian's request for enforcement is noted. Since the case has been appealed, the request will be temporarily delayed. ▲ Chen Hongsheng's request for deferring payment is noted. Since the payment has been limited in court, the request for deferral cannot be granted. ▲ Cui Tangshi's request for arrest and pursuit is noted and will be handled accordingly. ▲ Chen Zhifeng's payment and request for extending the payment period by two months are noted. The payment of 5 yuan is received and will be held for the creditor to collect. The remaining amount should be paid within two weeks and no further delays will be allowed. ▲ Zhou Zongbao's request for prompt sealing is noted and has been ordered for implementation. ▲ Shen Guokang's request for collecting the certificate is noted. The separation agreement and newspaper report are received. The requestor should bring the documents to the court on July 2 at 8:00 AM to collect the certificate. ▲ Xu Zisu's request for collecting the payment is noted. The requestor should bring the judgment to the court on July 5 at 9:00 AM to collect the payment. ▲ Ranji Foreign Goods Store et al.'s request for taking over the movable property and unsealing it is approved. ▲ Cao Liangxia's petition for enforcement is noted and will be followed up with summons for verification. ▲ Chen Bangyao's request for another summons is noted and will be handled after reviewing the case. ▲ Zhang Xigen et al.'s petition for enforcement is noted and will be followed up with strict pursuit after summons. ▲ Ding Jiesan's petition for enforcement is noted and will be followed up with interrogation and pursuit after summons. ▲ Huang Jialin's petition for canceling the case is approved. ▲ Ge Lugeng et al.'s petition for enforcement is noted and will be followed up with strict pursuit after summons. ▲ Liu Rongsheng's petition for enforcement is noted and will be followed up with strict pursuit after summons. ▲ Zhang Zhiren's petition for enforcement is noted. Since the case file has not been returned, the enforcement will be delayed. ▲ Zhang Jinkui et al.'s petition for auctioning is noted. Since an objection to this case has been raised, the request will be temporarily delayed. ▲ Ding Qiwen's request for suspending enforcement is approved. ▲ Wu Zhushi's petition for detaining the local guarantor is noted and will be followed up with summons for verification. ▲ Tang Songbai's petition for repairing the revetment is noted. The original judgment states that the appellant should leave a six-foot-wide passage to the south on the disputed land from the northeastern corner of the riverside, and does not include the riverside. The meaning is very clear. The petitioner's filling of the riverside revetment as part of the passage is not in accordance. The request for repairing the revetment is deemed unnecessary. ▲ Zhou Futian's petition for appointing a representative is approved. ▲ Tan Limin's petition for enforcement is noted and will be followed up with summons for enforcement. ▲ Yang Xianbang's request for appointing a representative is approved. ▲ Shao Nanji's petition for enforcement is noted. The Qingpu County government has been entrusted to enforce the judgment and has been urged. If the enforcement is insufficient to offset the debt, the guarantor should be responsible. The petitioner is informed accordingly. ▲ Xu Yutian's request for enforcement is noted and will be followed up with summons for pursuit. ▲ Wang Chunfu et al.'s request for extending the enforcement deadline by half a month is approved. ▲ Hou Fangde's request for enforcement is noted and will be followed up with summons for pursuit. ▲ Wang Quanlin's request for enforcement is noted and will be followed up with summons for pursuit. ▲ Wang Lishi's request for enforcement is noted. Since the case has been appealed, the request will be temporarily delayed. ▲ Ruan Changxing's request for continuing summons for enforcement is noted and will be followed up with further summons. ▲ Qiao Jianzhi's request for collecting the account books is approved. The requestor should bring the documents to the court on July 2 at 10:00 AM to collect the account books. ▲ Tan Fufu's petition for enforcement is noted. Since the file has not yet been sent, the request for enforcement will be delayed. ▲ He Jinlian's petition for enforcement is noted and will be followed up with summons for pursuit. ▲ Mao Fengzhi's petition for enforcement is noted and is approved for summons for interrogation and pursuit. ▲ Wang Zhiqing's petition for enforcement is noted and will be followed up with summons for pursuit. ▲ Zheng Shaolin's petition for enforcement is noted and will be followed up with summons for interrogation and pursuit. ▲ Zhu Zhenqing's petition for enforcement is noted and will be followed up with summons for interrogation and pursuit. ▲ Chen Gengxin's petition for enforcement is noted and will be followed up with summons for enforcement. ▲ Pan Chunming's petition for enforcement is noted and will be followed up with summons for enforcement. ▲ Lin Xintong's petition for enforcement is noted and will be followed up with summons for interrogation and pursuit.

Criminal Ruling: Regarding the case of Shen Yongming et al. for obstructing public order, assault, and robbery, the judges of this court requested an extension of the detention period. The detention of Jin Yaowen, Shen Yongming, Shen Yuelin, Shen Yongyongqing, Shen Fugeng, Xu Adi, Lei Youqing, and Zhu Biao is extended by two months. (June 28)
